RENTER BEWARE!!! In the 5 years my husband and I lived at Promenade Terrace, management changed 4 times!!! We have had our fair share of problems over the years... The ceiling collapsed and flooded our shower with water from a leak in the upstairs neighbors unit, our fridge went out multiple times and all our food went bad (while I was in labor with my son), the AC leaked inside the wall and water was trapped in the wall causing the wall to bubble up, along with many other things. I wanted to share a few issues because it wasn‚Äôt small things like ‚Äúoh I need a new light bulb‚Äù. However, the last straw was when I found out about the RATS living in the walls of our building. Yes you read that correct! Current management, Greystar, which changed their name or title right before we moved out is WELL AWARE of the ongoing rat infestation in my old building (521). Once I found out a rat had been in my home - I went to several neighbors and found out rats had already been in multiple of their homes as well. I found out from more residents that other buildings have had rats in their walls as well. It was heart wrenching for me, finding out as much as I did from others about the rat issues, about the overall lack of care from office staff and about the laundry list of maintenance orders that haven‚Äôt been done in months ‚Äúbecause of covid‚Äù (only emergency orders). Back to my story. The rats chewed through the insulation and wall creating a hole underneath the sink of my son‚Äôs bedroom! I found poop droppings throughout the house, even on my kitchen counter. I overnighted rat traps and set them in the cabinet underneath the sink and I duct taped the cabinet shut and we caught a rat that night. Check yelp review for photos! I pleaded to property management and to ‚ÄúThat Guy‚Äù pest control to do something about the rats in the walls!!! I found out the rats had been in the walls and entering into multiple houses of my building for a FULL YEAR. I asked them to wire a camera through the hole from my home to see how bad the infestation was! I asked them to tent the building and clear out all the possible dead rats in the walls and the toxic rat pee/poop. For the safety and well being of my family and all my neighbors. What did they do? Place bait, wait 1-2 days, come back and patch the hole and put more bait outside the building. That is all they do! Time and time again. It‚Äôs a case of PLAUSIBLE DENIABILITY. Within 24 hrs of opening the case, management contacted me to offer us to move to a different unit (for the same rent price we currently had) or to move-out with no penalty breaking our lease. <Text>Really enjoyed my meal! Price was great, food was tasty! It was my first experience with Ethiopian cuisine, so I can't speak to authenticity, but it was a nice experience.

I let them convince me to order my food at a 4 spiciness level instead of the 5 or 6 I originally asked for. It was delicious, but not the runny nose level I intended to order! I tend to prefer spicier foods though üòä. If you typically order spicey foods at Indian or Thai restaurants, you should be fine here too, similar spice scale.

If you're nervous to try something new, look up Ethiopian cuisine guides online and read a little about what to expect (what to order, how to eat, etc). Staff was nice, and can help you choose something!

Give it a try!!< /Text>< Name>

<Rating>1<//Rating>< text>
Ok so it's Sizzler. Food was fine. Devon at the counter, also fine. Minor thing: asked what to drink, I responded, "water, bubbly if you have it (as a lot of fast casual places now do)." Seated at the table, I see on my receipt I was charged almost three bucks for the water. I brought the bubbly water back to Devon without touching it, saying, you know, that's kind of a lot; I'll just have tap. I'm cool about it, he's cool about it, but it was an ordeal getting my card credited. Which it never was. I was charged $37, and then $34 again.
A manager (named Cho) happened to come by and cleared my salad plate, and asked me if everything was good. I responded "No."
She asked, "No?"
I again responded, "No."
Now it got strange. She walked away, never to return. I asked Devon on the way out whether I could speak to a manager. He explained that Cho was the manager. In fact he called her the owner. I was skeptical, but asked if I could speak to her again to resolve the double charge, and he replied that she was too busy.
I left, and tried calling the restaurant on my way home to see if I could be connected with anyone who could rectify the charge. I was connected with Cho. I'll spare you the details, but the conversation was theater of the absurd, and I remain overcharged. A call to Sizzler has gotten no response.
Bottom line: food here is fine, but good luck if anything goes wrong.<//text>
